                   <span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15">
                   </span>
                   <span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15">
                   </span>
                   <span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15">
                   </span>
                  </span>
                  <span class="greyText">
                   ·
                  </span>
                  <a class="lightGreyText" href="/book/show/21523103-harry-potter-and-the-philosopher-s-stone" title="Hardcover 9781408855898">
                   review of another edition
                  </a>
                 </div>
                 <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1053147591">
                   <span id="freeTextContainer11530922465134192866">
                    <b>
                     It's Always Great, Coming back Home..
                     <br>
                      <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="292" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411256402i/11211677._SX540_.jpg" width="470">
                       <br>
                        There's a reason us, the Fans, feel that we're connected, no matter where we from, different culture, ethics, ages..we're all graduated from there..
                        <br>
                         <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="305" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411258362i/11211797._SX540_.jpg" width="470">
                          <br>
                           ..Hogwarts.. even like we were in same class,classmates, no matter which edition we read..
                           <br>
                            <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="357" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411257184i/11211711._SX540_.jpg" width="470"/>
                            <br>
                             ..Cause Harry Potter is not just a story..it's a Life..
                             <br>
                              <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="264" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1472432297ra/20192894.gif" width="470"/>
                              <br>
                               <blockquote>
                                <u>
                                 The Boy Who
                                 <s>
                                  Saved
                                 </s>
                                 Flourished the Book Industry
                                </u>
                               </blockquote>
                              </br>
                             </br>
                            </br>
                           </br>
                          </br>
                         </img>
                        </br>
                       </br>
                      </img>
                     </br>
                    </b>
                    It's One of the most important novels in modern history, Sorry, it's
                    <b>
                     The Most Important ONE.
                    </b>
                    <br>
                     <i>
                      This Review also for those who
                     </i>
                    </br>
                   </span>
                   <span id="freeText11530922465134192866" style="display:none">
                    <b>
                     It's Always Great, Coming back Home..
                     <br/>
                     <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="292" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411256402i/11211677._SX540_.jpg" width="470"/>
                     <br/>
                     There's a reason us, the Fans, feel that we're connected, no matter where we from, different culture, ethics, ages..we're all graduated from there..
                     <br/>
                     <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="305" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411258362i/11211797._SX540_.jpg" width="470"/>
                     <br/>
                     ..Hogwarts.. even like we were in same class,classmates, no matter which edition we read..
                     <br/>
                     <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="357" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411257184i/11211711._SX540_.jpg" width="470"/>
                     <br/>
                     ..Cause Harry Potter is not just a story..it's a Life..
                     <br/>
                     <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="264" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1472432297ra/20192894.gif" width="470"/>
                     <br/>
                     <blockquote>
                      <u>
                       The Boy Who
                       <s>
                        Saved
                       </s>
                       Flourished the Book Industry
                      </u>
                     </blockquote>
                    </b>
                    It's One of the most important novels in modern history, Sorry, it's
                    <b>
                     The Most Important ONE.
                    </b>
                    <br/>
                    <i>
                     This Review also for those who hate the series !
                     <br/>
                     Please bear with me..
                    </i>
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Without it, most Book stores &amp; publishers may have the same fate of Video Stores like Blockbuster LLC, which, despite being super popular in the 90s, closed all the stores by 2013, shutting down forever.
                    <br/>
                    <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="250" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411425655i/11225976._SX540_.jpg" width="400"/>
                    <br/>
                    Yes, without this Novel, and with the rapid change in technology, the ease of making e-books and reading it in PCs, Smartphones, Tablets..etc, the publishing and trade of new paper books may decrease rapidly.
                    <br/>
                    It'd be limited for religious or educating books, classics, small novels. Even those could be just electronic too, and the Books be just like Good Ol' Video Tapes.
                    <br/>
                    <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="250" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411427520i/11226186._SX540_.jpg" width="400"/>
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    A Dystopia, right? very gloomy idea to the world without This novel,
                    <b>
                     The One.
                    </b>
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Well, in the case you think I'm exaggerate..Let's have,
                    <br/>
                    <blockquote>
                     <b>
                      A
                      <i>
                       Brief !!
                      </i>
                      History of Literature in the 90s
                      <br/>
                      -------------------------------
                     </b>
                    </blockquote>
                    Well, let’s back to early 90s , where TV is in every house, even in every room, Video sets are there too, rental video stores everywhere, satellite receivers and cable channels growing fast packed with channels for kids &amp; teenagers, making them attached more &amp; more into screens,
                    <i>
                     not to mention Video Games, Game boy and Nintendo
                    </i>
                    …
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Those of this new generation who read are “weirdos" or "nerds” to the rest of their peers.
                    <br/>
                    And for those “few who read”, book stores mostly got for them comics and graphic novels, which most of them created early this century.
                    <br/>
                    <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="350" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411429565i/11226560._SY540_.jpg" width="400"/>
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Classic Novels, they read just for Schools and Classes mostly.
                    <br/>
                    And New Novels that make Best Seller are the ones made, or will be made, into movies for Julia Roberts, Tom Cruse or any of the 90s Hollywood celebrity, or the ones by Stephen King because ,of course, will be made into movies too.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Even these new novels didn't live up the selling numbers of Tolkien, Charles Dickens, Agatha Christie
                    <i>
                     -what’s with the British authors and selling numbers :)?-
                    </i>
                    , also in Russia no more Dostoevsky and Tolstoy, no more Hugo in France, in
                    <b>
                     Egypt
                    </b>
                    no more like Naguib Mahfouz &amp; the great authors of the 50s to 70s..
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    No new Big Hit for novels, most of the selling books are those of Speculation about strange &amp; mysterious things in the world or in religion, Dream interpretation , cocking books or celebrities rumors.
                    <br/>
                    <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="350" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411582524i/11251816._SX540_.jpg" width="400"/>
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    While in US &amp; UK, Top Selling books mostly the Self Help ones, or those teaching Computers Programming and Web Sites
                    <i>
                     -this brand new huge technology leap back then-
                    </i>
                    <br/>
                    <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="174" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411584118i/11252020._SX540_.jpg" width="401"/>
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    No new novels to attract the new generation of kids and teenagers, There's few Successful Highlights though, like R.L.Stine’s Goosepumbs in 1992 which made a very good success, and translated in many countries including Egypt.
                    <br/>
                    <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="188" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411584118i/11252021._SX540_.jpg" width="400"/>
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    And in Egypt there’s also a very successful project by respectful Publishing house that made “Pocket Novels” for youth, by brilliant Egyptian writers presenting huge variety of novels of many genres, Sci-Fi, Action Thriller, comics, Romance .etc.
                    <br/>
                    <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="250" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411584118i/11252022._SX540_.jpg" width="401"/>
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    There’s also “Reading for All”, project by the first lady “Susan Mubarak”, reprinting a huge verity of important books and novels from all over the world in very cheap prices.
                    <br/>
                    <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="274" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411584576i/11252145._SX540_.jpg" width="401"/>
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    But all these effort didn't attract “more and more” of new youth readers as intended, it just made more and more books for those few who already reads.
                    <br/>
                    The vast numbers of those who don’t just read will increase if there isn't a BIG new attractive
                    <b>
                     Reading Experience
                    </b>
                    to get them into reading, specially with the more channels, more movies.
                    <br/>
                    But the BIGGEST Obstacle for them to read came out in
                    <b>
                     1994
                    </b>
                    , and became a real phenomenon by 1995..
                    <br/>
                    <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="220" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411611859i/11255857._SX540_.jpg" width="400"/>
                    <br/>
                    ..it’s
                    <b>
                     Playstation
                    </b>
                    , The giant Japanese Gaming leap..
                    <br/>
                    Football, Crash, Pepsi man, even the comics heroes also have their games, so why reading Superman, Batman’s comics when you can play them..
                    <br/>
                    <blockquote>
                     <i>
                      ~~~~~~ A beat. ~~~~~~
                     </i>
                    </blockquote>
                    <br/>
                    So by 1996, with this growing leap in Gaming, also the Computer 3D games getting much improved, Books get replaced bit by bit by a gaming controls.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    So do you think it’s wise for publishers to publish a book for new writer?
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Of course not, it may not even cover it’s publishing cost.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    So it was very normal when in this year, 1996, when
                    <b>
                     Joanne
                    </b>
                    , a 31 years old lady from England , handed the manuscript of her first novel to 12 publishing houses, all of them rejected it...
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    A manuscript of over 200 pages of a novel,
                    <i>
                     that she had hard times in her personal and professional life while writing it,
                    </i>
                    and for children??? Seriously is there still any Child left who still read? it’s 1996, the Era of Playstation and Video Games.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    But then, the Modest
                    <b>
                     “Bloomsbury“
                    </b>
                    agreed to publish it , with 2 advises for her, first that she’d get a day job, since it’s a little chance of making money in children's books.
                    <i>
                     - later she received a grant from the Scottish Arts Council to help her continuing writing.-
                    </i>
                    <br/>
                    But the significant advice was to change her pen name cause young boys might not want to read a book written by a woman..
                    <br/>
                    So with her name &amp; her grandmother’s "Kathleen" come the 2 initial of her pen name..
                    <br/>
                    <blockquote>
                     <b>
                      J . k . Rowling
                     </b>
                    </blockquote>
                    <br/>
                    And in
                    <b>
                     26 June 1997
                    </b>
                    , with 1,000 copies, 500 of which were distributed to libraries, come out in UK, to our World The Greatest..
                    <br/>
                    <blockquote>
                     <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="720" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411626851i/11258422._SY540_.jpg" width="333"/>
                     <b>
                      <br/>
                      Harry Potter and the Philosopher's Stone
                     </b>
                    </blockquote>
                    <br/>
                    And Bam!! , everything happened so fast..
                    <br/>
                    Before the end of this year the novel was awarded many important literary awards in the UK.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    An American important publisher, Scholastic, won the rights to publish the novel in US, with a huge check Rowling would never dreams of.
                    <br/>
                    Just with small change, 'Philosopher's Stone' to be 'Sorcerer's Stone', as the American publisher feared 'Philosopher's' may not be that attractive to young readers..
                    <br/>
                    <i>
                     And Thanks to Harry Potter, now Every young readers worldwide know much more about Philosopher's Stone's legend.
                    </i>
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    In
                    <b>
                     1998
                    </b>
                    Book Two released in UK ,
                    <b>
                     1999
                    </b>
                    in US, winning more literary prizes. And becoming NO.1 Top Selling Book in UK , US and many other countries which start to publish the translated first book.
                    <br/>
                    <blockquote>
                     <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="280" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411667189i/11263200.jpg" width="363"/>
                    </blockquote>
                    And on
                    <b>
                     8 July 1999
                    </b>
                    , The
                    <b>
                     <u>
                      First Breaking Record
                     </u>
                    </b>
                    made when Book Three sold
                    <b>
                     68.000 copies
                    </b>
                    in just three days after its release in the United Kingdom.. and more copies when it released late 1999 in US..
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    With the fast growing popularity of Harry Potter among readers, more records had been broken..
                    <br/>
                    <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="300" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411659710i/11262277._SX540_.jpg" width="400"/>
                    <br/>
                    The 3 books takeover the Top Spot in all charts of Best Selling Books for weeks &amp; months, and it's even still in hardcover editions.
                    <br/>
                    This conquer of the Top Spots made some literary magazines &amp; newspapers separate the 'Harry Potter books' selling records from the rest of the top selling books, splitting the lists into 'Children Books' and 'Adult Books' sections, under pressure from other publishers who were eager to see their books given higher ranking.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    <b>
                     And then it was year 2000 , where everything is about to change ... forever..
                    </b>
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    The Playstation 2 is out there, and even higher leap in Computer Games..
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    But even with this much of temptations, thousands of children, teens and parents gathered in the Midnight of
                    <b>
                     8 July 2000
                    </b>
                    in UK and US at the same day in front of stores, not in front of Cinemas as usual, not electronic stores as Apple stores
                    <i>
                     as happening theses days
                    </i>
                    , But it was in front of
                    <b>
                     Bookstores
                    </b>
                    , for The First time in the Book Stores History, to buy a copy of...
                    <br/>
                    <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="283" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411670472i/11263478._SX540_.jpg" width="430"/>
                    <br/>
                    <b>
                     Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire
                    </b>
                    <br/>
                    And They didn't mind to find out that the book is over 700 page, it was even for their pleasure, more than double the size of any of the first 3 novels.. double the thriller, double the fun..
                    <br/>
                    <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="282" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411670796i/11263575._SX540_.jpg" width="430"/>
                    <br/>
                    Over 3 million copies sold at that day only in the US , a New World Record, totally unexpected one.
                    <br/>
                    Huge story, bigger plot , mysterious and very well written.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    And more literate prizes for Rowling... more translated editions to more than 40 language.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    And a huge budget for the upcoming first movie of the series, which beautifully visualize the magic of the novel by the faithful producers and the director...and it also made some Cinematic Records back then,
                    <i>
                     but that's not our subject now
                    </i>
                    .
                    <br/>
                    <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="300" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411757596i/11270149.jpg" width="400"/>
                    <br/>
                    <blockquote>
                     <i>
                      ~~~~~~ ~~~~~~
                     </i>
                    </blockquote>
                    <br/>
                    With the announcement of pushing the publishing date of Book Five to mid. 2003 , and with 2 movies out so far, The Hunger for reading Harry Potter kept on..
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    So, As more readers from this generation start to increase , Publishers and Book Stores start to promote for more books for those readers who are hungry for more..
                    <br/>
                    Older Fantasy books , like Lord of the Rings
                    <i>
                     -which was a super successful movie by then too-
                    </i>
                    Narnia , Golden Compass and many other novels start getting more reprinted editions. And so Book Stores prosperity increased as it get more and more readers.
                    <br/>
                    <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="224" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411757596i/11270150._SX540_.jpg" width="400"/>
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    More countries welcomed the Harry Potter phenomenon.. The English edition AND the local translated ones , both been sold everywhere worldwide.
                    <br/>
                    <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="186" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411757596i/11270151._SX540_.png" width="400"/>
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Even in
                    <b>
                     Egypt
                    </b>
                    English edition sold at many books stores. And, hopefully, some New Book Stores specialized in English novels and books start to open in Cairo &amp; Alexandria by 2002-2003..
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    And in summer 2002, after the Movie wild success, Nahdet Masr publishing house got the rights and published the Arabic edition.
                    <br/>
                    Although it cut some of the lines for length issues, the edition still hold the magic of it ..making a very good sales.
                    <br/>
                    <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="300" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411758298i/11270181.jpg" width="400"/>
                    <br/>
                    <blockquote>
                     <i>
                      ~~~~~~ ~~~~~~
                     </i>
                    </blockquote>
                    <br/>
                    The good news is, the literary movement didn't stop there, Harry Potter and Reprinted Classics. No , there's more new books come out for the increasing demand from the readers..
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    By
                    <b>
                     2002
                    </b>
                    ,
                    <b>
                     Life of Pi
                    </b>
                    , Man Booker winner make very good sales numbers.
                    <br/>
                    <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="200" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411757596i/11270152._SX540_.jpg" width="401"/>
                    <br/>
                    And in
                    <b>
                     April 2003
                    </b>
                    Dan Brown
                    <i>
                     (previously published 3 novels, making good sales)
                    </i>
                    released a novel that made Huge Fuss around and making a new sales records,
                    <b>
                     The Da Vinci Code
                    </b>
                    ..
                    <br/>
                    <i>
                     The funny thing that there's a reference in this novel that Harry Potter is '
                    </i>
                    the Second Most Selling Book in History after the Bible
                    <i>
                     ', a speculation that happens to be true in less than 5 years after that.
                    </i>
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    A month later,
                    <b>
                     May 2003
                    </b>
                    , Khaled Hosseini released his first novel,
                    <b>
                     The Kate Runner
                    </b>
                    which also made a very good records too.
                    <i>
                     -Don't you agree if there's no Harry Potter before, this Afghan-born author would have a chance? He'd be rejected by 12 publishers like you know who :)-
                    </i>
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    And all that didn't affect the main reason for this new 'Literal Renaissance'.
                    <br/>
                    All that didn't affect the Records Breaker to break records one month later..
                    <br/>
                    <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="290" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411758082i/11270171._SX540_.jpg" width="400"/>
                    <br/>
                    On
                    <b>
                     20 June 2003
                    </b>
                    book Five
                    <b>
                     'Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix'
                    </b>
                    comes out..
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Ten thousands of all ages conquer the Book Stores in UK, US and other countries too at the same day to get The One Book they've been waiting for at least 2 years. Shipping agents like FedEx made the delivery to many countries to get the book at the same time.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    <b>
                     A New world Record
                    </b>
                    ,5 millions copy at the first day only..
                    <br/>
                    For the first time in France a non french language book placed in no.1 of the bestselling book....
                    <br/>
                    <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="242" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411758082i/11270172._SX540_.jpg" width="430"/>
                    <br/>
                    Some kids got a headache called 'Harry Potter Headache' as they read the whole 850 pages of the book five, the biggest so far, at the same day without resting.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    And in
                    <b>
                     Egypt
                    </b>
                    , September the same year, the Arabic edition of book three comes out with unexpected sales records, first edition run out of the stores by the first week only, though it's nearly the beginning of the School year, and the movie of this 3rd book still filming.
                    <br/>
                    ِAnd the price of it get higher 20% in 2 days and still with increasing demand..
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    More English books and novels sold in Egypt too, along with the Arabic ones, publishing more books for new Egyptian authors and writers along with more of the famous ones, Alaa El Aswany's debut Novel 'Yaqubean's Building' making a very good selling numbers..
                    <br/>
                    <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2347744.______________" rel="nofollow noopener" title="عمارة يعقوبيان by Alaa Al Aswany">
                     <img alt="عمارة يعقوبيان by Alaa Al Aswany" class="gr-hostedUserImg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1330808486s/2347744.jpg"/>
                    </a>
                    <br/>
                    And in
                    <b>
                     July 2004
                    </b>
                    the Arabic edition of Book Four makes a price war between book stores and magazines stands.
                    <br/>
                    <b>
                     January 2005
                    </b>
                    , an abridged translated edition of Book Five make many readers angry in Egypt , specially that many already read the English edition before, so the publisher release an unabridged one by May.
                    <br/>
                    <blockquote>
                     <i>
                      ~~~~~~ ~~~~~~
                     </i>
                    </blockquote>
                    <br/>
                    And on
                    <b>
                     21 July 2005
                    </b>
                    ,
                    <b>
                     A Higher Record
                    </b>
                    that breaks all the previously ones
                    <br/>
                    <blockquote>
                     <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="500" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411759919i/11270289.jpg" width="344"/>
                    </blockquote>
                    <br/>
                    6.9 million copy of Book Six sold in US in its first day only...
                    <br/>
                    A huge book, it may not be as the fans' expectations of being full of action , but it get a twist that blow minds about one of the most interesting characters,
                    <b>
                     Professor Snape.
                    </b>
                    That made many fans and even big authors like Stephen King and Salman Rushdie talk about for months..
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    With Pre-Final Book of Harry Potter is out, it followed by a massive variety of New Novels, New Series, New Authors..
                    <br/>
                    <b>
                     Twilight series, Percy Jackson series
                    </b>
                    , and much more, more Books Sales not only in US, UK but worldwide..
                    <br/>
                    More Novels hit the top sales..
                    <br/>
                    A Real Prosperity.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    But still Harry Potter is the Records Big Breaker...
                    <br/>
                    <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="285" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411781936i/11273744._SX540_.jpg" width="430"/>
                    <br/>
                    At the midnight before
                    <b>
                     21 June 2007
                    </b>
                    , Everywhere around the Globe, the scene of thousands of people lining in front of Book Stores was repeated...even Bigger than any time before..
                    <br/>
                    <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="269" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411781936i/11273745.jpg" width="430"/>
                    <br/>
                    A Huge Record for Pre-Orders online reach to One Million copies by Amazon only, and total sales of
                    <b>
                     11 millions copies in UK and US in the first day only.
                    </b>
                    <br/>
                    <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="275" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411781936i/11273746._SX540_.jpg" width="430"/>
                    <br/>
                    The book sold at the Same Day almost in Every Single Country..
                    <br/>
                    <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="517" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480705819i/21341831._SY540_.jpg" width="430"/>
                    <br/>
                    <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="344" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480705819i/21341832._SX540_.jpg" width="430"/>
                    <br/>
                    even in Israel which made a big religious fuss because the Book Stores opened to receive and sell the book at the releasing day which was their holy Saturday, But it's Harry Potter after all, the world's most unusual, unexpected phenomenon and sales records breaker.
                    <br/>
                    <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="313" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411781936i/11273747.jpg" width="430"/>
                    <br/>
                    And that's not bad, it was the Miracle of bringing back readers to Book Stores...
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    And it's not just Harry Potter...
                    <br/>
                    Now, that
                    <b>
                     <i>
                      'All was well.'
                     </i>
                    </b>
                    , thousands of topics went online asking 'what to read next'....
                    <br/>
                    Indeed, although there's the e-books, e-readers..etc, still there's thousands of new books and novels published and sold every year , in every where in the world.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    The gaming devices is increasing? yes, But not as expected though by the 90s and early 2000s
                    <i>
                     'remember Nokia N-Gage?'
                    </i>
                    .. but so does the reading devices which first come out by Sony in 2004,make big step by Amazon's Kindle in 2007...the ebook applications on every device.
                    <br/>
                    <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="218" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411835645i/11285409._SX540_.jpg" width="400"/>
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    New books and series come after that, and still on, making super sales, attracting more readers... more writers come with more books and novels, some are just a rip off others and some are really original and brilliant. in UK, US , Egypt ..everywhere all over the globe..
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    No matter a Playstation 4 is out, or new Xbox, the Books still there...with its most beloved magic..
                    <br/>
                    <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="218" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411835645i/11285410.jpg" width="400"/>
                    <br/>
                    The magic of books is back and , I believe, to stay..
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Don't you see with me that the magic of Harry Potter is one of the main factors of this magic?
                    <br/>
                    <blockquote>
                     <b>
                      <br/>
                      “This boy will be famous. There won’t be a child in our world who doesn’t know his name”
                      <br/>
                      <img class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="260" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411836005i/11285585.jpg" width="400"/>
                     </b>
                    </blockquote>
                    <br/>
                    That's what Rowling wrote at the very early pages of her first book.. The one that rejected by 12 Publishing Houses in 1996..
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Well, what about now?
                    <br/>
                    <i>
                     <br/>
                     God, Talked too much in the "Brief" introduction , didn't I?
                     <br/>
                    </i>
                    <br/>
                    Well, that's it for this review... I guess some still think it's just the Propaganda that made that all....
                    <br/>
                    Well I'll try to prove them wrong by the upcoming next 6 reviews at the other 6 Books of the series..
                    <br/>
                    Links will be here as soon as it'd done ..
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    But for The First one... sorry to add one more , but 20000 characters aren't enough.
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1426951998" rel="nofollow noopener">
                     The Ultimate Review of Book One
                    </a>
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Now I'll be back to go around Hogwarts...
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    <img alt="0" class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="273" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411082784i/11192136._SX540_.jpg" width="400"/>
                    <br/>
                    For the Zillionth time I guess..
                    <br/>
                    <img alt="0" class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="197" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411082784i/11192137._SX540_.jpg" width="400"/>
                    <br/>
                    Hope to see you there too, come on and try first year :)
                    <br/>
                    <img alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="315" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380396313i/763769.jpg" width="395"/>
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    From Hogwarts
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Mohammed Arabey
                    <br/>
                    The Craziest Potterhead of Egypt
                    <br/>
                    <img alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg" height="217" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1381936688i/5444084.jpg" width="401"/>
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    Re-reading the new edition -Guess I'm addicted to new editions BUT this one really rocks.."Bloomsbury-2014"
                    <br/>
                    from 12 Sep. 2014
                    <br/>
                    to 23 Sep. 2014
                    <br/>
                    <br/>
                    <a href="http://www.khassab.net/news/?p=3444" rel="nofollow noopener">
                     المقال بالعربية من هنا
                    </a>

                 <img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1628842961p2/69106439.jpg"/>
                </a>
                <div class="left bodycol">
                 <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
                  <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2047870291?book_show_action=true">
                   Nov 16, 2019
                  </a>
                  <span itemprop="author" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
                   <a class="user" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥">
                    Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥
                   </a>
                  </span>
                  rated it
                  <span class="staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing">
                   <span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15">
                    it was amazing
                   </span>
                   <span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15">
                   </span>
                   <span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15">

                  <a class="lightGreyText" href="/book/show/1885731.Harry_Potter_and_the_Philosopher_s_Stone" title="Paperback 9780747549550">
                   review of another edition
                  </a>
                  <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
                   Shelves:
                   <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale?shelf=favorites">
                    favorites
                   </a>

                 <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer2047870291">
                   <span id="freeTextContainer10380817257413812072">
                    I have absolutley no idea why goodreads deleted my review AND rating but thankfully I still had it saved! So here it is again, may it stick around this time!
                    <br>
                     <br>
                      <i>
                       ”It does not do to dwell on dreams and forget to live, remember that.”
                      </i>
                      <br>
                       <br>
                        Okay, here’s the thing: There are already 96.502 reviews about this book on goodreads and I think it’s safe to say that mine will carry no weight. *lol*
                        <br>
                         So I decided to make this a short “my thoughts about this book” review. ;-P
                         <br>
                          <br>
                           1.)
                           <i>
                            ”Thirty-six,” he said, looking up at his
                           </i>
                          </br>
                         </br>
                        </br>
                       </br>
                      </br>
                     </br>
                    </br>
                   </span>
                   <span id="freeText10380817257413812072" style="display:none">
                    I have absolutley no idea why goodreads deleted my review AND rating but thankfully I still had it saved! So here it is again, may it stick around this time!
                    <br>
                     <br>
                      <i>
                       ”It does not do to dwell on dreams and forget to live, remember that.”
                      </i>
                      <br>
                       <br>
                        Okay, here’s the thing: There are already 96.502 reviews about this book on goodreads and I think it’s safe to say that mine will carry no weight. *lol*
                        <br>
                         So I decided to make this a short “my thoughts about this book” review. ;-P
                         <br>
                          <br>
                           1.)
                           <i>
                            ”Thirty-six,” he said, looking up at his mother and father. “That’s two less than last year.”
                           </i>
                           <br>
                            <br>
                             I totally forgot how horrible the Dursleys are and I think I kind of suppressed how dreadful Dudley is! Such a spoilt brat and this is actually putting it more than just lightly. If anyone should go to a boot camp sort of school it certainly should be him.
                             <br>
                              <br>
                               2.)
                               <i>
                                ”Ah, go boil yer heads, both of yeh,” said Hagrid. “Harry – yer a wizard.”
                               </i>
                               <br>
                                <br>
                                 Bless Hagrid for being the kind and compassionate man that he is! &lt;3 Those lines went down in Harry Potter history and started it all! XD
                                 <br>
                                  <br>
                                   3.)
                                   <i>
                                    ”Blown up a toilet? We’ve never blown up a toilet.”
                                    <br>
                                     “Great idea though, thanks, Mum.”
                                    </br>
                                   </i>
                                   <br>
                                    <br>
                                     Haha! You gotta love the Weasley twins! They might be side characters but they always manage to bring some humour into the book and they succeed to give that typical sibling and family vibe. =)
                                     <br>
                                      <br>
                                       4.)
                                       <i>
                                        ”Are you sure that’s a real spell?” said the girl. “Well, it’s not very good, is it? I’ve tried a few simple spells just for practice and it’s all worked for me.”
                                       </i>
                                       <br>
                                        <br>
                                         When I read this I totally had the Hermione of the movie in my mind. Emma Watson played her so well and I’m really glad that Hermione came off her high horse. She was really insufferable at the beginning of the book. *lol*
                                         <br>
                                          <br>
                                           5.)
                                           <i>
                                            ”You’ll soon find out some wizarding families are much better than others, Potter. You don’t want to go making friends with the wrong sort. I can help you there.”
                                           </i>
                                           <br>
                                            <br>
                                             Urgh! And so it begins! I never liked Malfoy and I’ll never do. Sorry, guys! Yes, I felt sorry for him after book 5 but he’s still a slimy little spoilt brat at the beginning of the series. Still, if his parents would have raised him differently he might have even turned out to be a nice guy. *sighs*
                                             <br>
                                              <br>
                                               6.)
                                               <i>
                                                ”Let’s try again. Potter, where would you look if I told you to find me a bezoar?”
                                               </i>
                                               <br>
                                                <br>
                                                 And here comes another character I’ll never forgive. Snape is a horrible teacher and an even worse human being. There I said it. Nothing that happens over the course of the following books will change anything about the fact that he’s unfair and mean to his students! His past doesn’t excuse his actions. Still, I gotta give Rowling kudos for all the foreboding! Boy, alone the comment with the bezoar. XD And Dumbledore explaining the relationship between Snape and Harry’s father. Well done! ;-)
                                                 <br>
                                                  <br>
                                                   7.)
                                                   <i>
                                                    ”But from that moment on, Hermione Granger became their friend. There are some things you can’t share without ending up liking each other, and knocking out a twelve-foot mountain troll is one of them.”
                                                   </i>
                                                   <br>
                                                    <br>
                                                     I still love that scene and I’m really glad Hermione and the others finally bonded. Also, I love that they tried to be good kids at the beginning. In the first book they actually don’t want to do anything forbidden and feel bad about it. Well, and then the other books happen. *LOL* Apparently practice makes perfect though, because they go for plenty of forbidden things but don’t get caught anymore. Haha!
                                                     <br>
                                                      <br>
                                                       8.)
                                                       <i>
                                                        ”All right, all right. Flint nearly kills the Gryffindor Seeker, which could happen to anyone, I’m sure, so a penalty to Gryffindor, taken by Spinnet, who puts it away, no trouble, and we continue play, Gryffindor still in possession.”
                                                       </i>
                                                       <br>
                                                        <br>
                                                         Lee Jordan is the best! &lt;3 He’s the main reason I enjoy the Quidditch games so much! His commentary is just funny and brilliant!
                                                         <br>
                                                          <br>
                                                           9.)
                                                           <i>
                                                            ”If I get caught before I can get to the Stone, well, I’ll have to go back to the Dursleys and wait for Voldemort to find me there. It’s only dying a bit later than I would have done, because I’m never going over to the Dark Side!”
                                                           </i>
                                                           <br>
                                                            <br>
                                                             I LOVE HARRY’S DEFIANCE!!! That’s one of the many things that made me like him so much! He never backs down and always continues to fight. No matter the odds, he’s facing his troubles holding his head high! Even this early in the series you can already see that he’s going to be a great MC!
                                                             <br>
                                                              <br>
                                                               And now let’s move on and read book two! ;-)
                                                              </br>
                                                             </br>
                                                            </br>
                                                           </br>
                                                          </br>
                                                         </br>
                                                        </br>
                                                       </br>
                                                      </br>
                                                     </br>
                                                    </br>
                                                   </br>

               <div class="review nosyndicate" id="review_46540413" itemprop="reviews" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
                <link href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/46540413" itemprop="url"/>
                <a class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen" title="Stephen">
                 <img alt="Stephen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311616811p2/1413439.jpg"/>
                </a>
                <div class="left bodycol">
                 <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
                  <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/46540413?book_show_action=true">
                   Feb 16, 2009
                  </a>
                  <span itemprop="author" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
                   <a class="user" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen" itemprop="url" name="Stephen" title="Stephen">
                    Stephen
                   </a>
                  </span>
                  rated it
                  <span class="staticStars notranslate" title="liked it">
                   <span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15">
                    liked it
                   </span>
                   <span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15">
                   </span>
                   <span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15">
                   </span>
                   <span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15">
                   </span>
                   <span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15">
                   </span>
                  </span>
                  <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
                   Shelves:
                   <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=fantasy">
                    fantasy
                   </a>
                   ,
                   <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=ya">
                    ya
                   </a>
                   ,
                   <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=1990-1999">
                    1990-1999
                   </a>
                   ,
                   <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=potteresque">
                    potteresque
                   </a>
                   ,
                   <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=comfort-food">
                    comfort-food
                   </a>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                 <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer46540413">
                   <span id="freeTextContainer13349744992619073391">
                    On my list of
                    <b>
                     reasons
                    </b>
                    why
                    <b>
                     my daughters
                    </b>
                    are the
                    <b>
                     bestest thing
                    </b>
                    to ever happen to me,
                    <b>
                     Number 14,577
                    </b>
                    is that they gave me, at
                    <b>
                     41 years old
                    </b>
                    , the perfect
                    <b>
                     excuse
                    </b>
                    to revisit the
                    <b>
                     Harry Potter
                    </b>
                    series.
                    <br>
                     <br>
                      When my oldest angel told me she wanted to start reading the Harry Potter books, I couldn’t have been happier. As I was collecting all seven volumes off the shelf to bring up to her room, I started feeling nostalgic for the whole Hogwarts gang, and I realized that I’d never done more than a perfunctory revie
                     </br>
                    </br>
                   </span>
                   <span id="freeText13349744992619073391" style="display:none">
                    On my list of
                    <b>
                     reasons
                    </b>
                    why
                    <b>
                     my daughters
                    </b>
                    are the
                    <b>
                     bestest thing
                    </b>
                    to ever happen to me,
                    <b>
                     Number 14,577
                    </b>
                    is that they gave me, at
                    <b>
                     41 years old
                    </b>
                    , the perfect
                    <b>
                     excuse
                    </b>
                    to revisit the
                    <b>
                     Harry Potter
                    </b>
                    series.
                    <br>
                     <br>
                      When my oldest angel told me she wanted to start reading the Harry Potter books, I couldn’t have been happier. As I was collecting all seven volumes off the shelf to bring up to her room, I started feeling nostalgic for the whole Hogwarts gang, and I realized that I’d never done more than a perfunctory review of this first volume. I figured it was high time to rectify that oversight.
                      <br>
                       <br>
                        Harry deserves it.
                        <br>
                         <br>
                          However, with over a million ratings, and almost two reviews for every day I’ve been alive, I think I can dispense with any plot distillation or character profiles. It has all been eloquently said before. Therefore, I just want to briefly express what I see as the essential magic at the heart of the series, and why I think it has resonated so strongly with so many people.
                          <br>
                           <br>
                            Here goes...
                            <br>
                             <br>
                              Only rarely does a story come along that can so completely wrap you up in a warm blanket of contentment and good feelings. One that can hold at bay, even if only for precious moments, the nasty brutishness of what often passes for daily life. These stories do that.
                              <br>
                               <br>
                                It’s an escape into a world of optimism, honor, and hope, where things always look hopeful and anything is possible. Who wouldn't want to hang around in a place like that, especially when it is decorated with sorting hats, kindly giants, magic wands and Quidditch.
                                <br>
                                 <br>
                                  Granted...no aspect of the story is revolutionary, or even particularly noteworthy, from the standpoint of blazing new trails within the fantasy genre. It isn’t great literature, and nothing about its technical merits makes it befitting of even a fraction of its unprecedented success.
                                  <br>
                                   <br>
                                    Fine...acknowledged. And? So what!
                                    <br>
                                     <br>
                                      The virtue of this story is the postive feelings it conjures in its readers. Harry’s story is something that radiates acceptance, inclusion, and friendship. It invokes a sense of belonging. Inside these pages, you can find the impetus to see the better angels of humanity’s nature, and feel just a little better about the world around you.
                                      <br>
                                       <br>
                                        How is that not worthy of praise?
                                        <br>
                                         <br>
                                          As for Harry himself, he’s just a good kid. The quintessential everyman who makes good. A loving boy with a clear head on his shoulders and a caring heart that pumps affection for the world around him. He’s someone you can’t help but like.
                                          <br>
                                           <br>
                                            He’s not perfect. He makes mistakes, he’s occasionally short sighted, and I know many of us wish he would stick up for himself a little more. Maybe reduce his aunt and uncle to a pair of fatty stains on the carpet, or give Dudley an atomic wedgie until his skivvies scrape against his pancreas.
                                            <br>
                                             <br>
                                              But that’s not Harry. He’s a better person than that. That’s why we love him.
                                              <br>
                                               <br>
                                                Maybe all of the above is a bit much. Like I said, I was feeling nostalgic and maybe the gush got a tad away from me. Let’s just say that these stories are perfect comfort food and reading them will make you happy.
                                                <br>
                                                 <br>
                                                  I’ll certainly settle for that.
                                                  <br>
                                                   <br>
                                                    As for the rating, I Initially only gave this first volume 3 stars, and I’m not going to change that now. As much as I love the series as a whole, I don’t think it reaches stratospheric heights until
                                                    <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6.Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire__Harry_Potter___4_" rel="nofollow noopener" title="Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire (Harry Potter, #4) by J.K. Rowling">
                                                     Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire
                                                    </a>
                                                    .
                                                    <br>
                                                     <br>
                                                      Still, this is where it all began. As such, it should be read and savored knowing that it only gets better.
                                                      <br>
                                                       <br>
                                                        3.0 stars. Highly Recommended.
                                                        <br/>
                                                       </br>
                                                      </br>
                                                     </br>

               <div class="review" id="review_4380321427" itemprop="reviews" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
                <link href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/4380321427" itemprop="url"/>
                <a class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/124132123-lisa-of-troy" title="Lisa of Troy">
                 <img alt="Lisa of Troy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605150099p2/124132123.jpg"/>
                </a>
                <div class="left bodycol">
                 <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
                  <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/4380321427?book_show_action=true">
                   Jan 14, 2022
                  </a>
                  <span itemprop="author" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
                   <a class="user" href="/user/show/124132123-lisa-of-troy" itemprop="url" name="Lisa of Troy" title="Lisa of Troy">
                    Lisa of Troy
                   </a>
                  </span>
                  rated it
                  <span class="staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing">
                   <span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15">
                    it was amazing
                   </span>
                   <span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15">
                   </span>
                   <span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15">
                   </span>
                   <span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15">
                   </span>
                   <span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15">
                   </span>
                  </span>
                 </div>
                 <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer4380321427">
                   <span id="freeTextContainer6304863612102536853">
                    <b>
                     These Are The Stories Before We Had SmartPhones
                    </b>
                    <br>
                     <br>
                      Many years ago, I read Harry Potter and the Sorcerer's Stone when it was first published in the US, before the movie, before all of the fame and merchandising opportunities. Initially, when I read it, I devoured it in two days. Now that I am old, well as old as Megan Fox, I wanted to hate on the author but couldn't.
                      <br>
                       <br>
                        JK Rowling makes writing look easy. Her prose is easy to read out loud, very smooth. Although the world that she has created is magical,
                       </br>
                      </br>
                     </br>
                    </br>
                   </span>
                   <span id="freeText6304863612102536853" style="display:none">
                    <b>
                     These Are The Stories Before We Had SmartPhones
                    </b>
                    <br>
                     <br>
                      Many years ago, I read Harry Potter and the Sorcerer's Stone when it was first published in the US, before the movie, before all of the fame and merchandising opportunities. Initially, when I read it, I devoured it in two days. Now that I am old, well as old as Megan Fox, I wanted to hate on the author but couldn't.
                      <br>
                       <br>
                        JK Rowling makes writing look easy. Her prose is easy to read out loud, very smooth. Although the world that she has created is magical, it isn't confusing or that difficult to imagine unlike LOTR or Dune. The book is also incredibly fast paced. Many of the fantasy books that I have read have at least 100 pages to warm up. So how does the author make us want to root or cheer for Harry? How do we become invested in him? He is an orphan and an abused orphan at that. On the one hand, this formula definitely works, but isn't it a little over done? JK Rowling also sets up some beautiful scenes like when Harry is receiving his invitation to Hogwarts. How many people actually try that hard? When Ron and Harry discover that Hermione is in danger, they both go to assist her. However, most people these days would go, "Oh well." Sorry my INFJ is showing.
                        <br>
                         <br>
                          There were a few things that I didn't like:
                          <br>
                           *Why does JK Rowling hate cats? Mr Dursley sees something odd, a cat reading a map. My cats play chess, play the piano, watch TV, and once even typed "hi" on my computer. I don't find reading a map to be a bit strange at all. Maybe my house is just brimming with magic and as a muggle I just don't know about it? Mrs. Figg also made Harry look at photographs of all of the cats that she has ever owned. As if that is some sort of punishment!
                           <br>
                            *How Hermione is treated. When Ron and Harry are in trouble, Ron screams at her, "Have you gone mad? Are you a witch or not?" Um Ron, if you treat me like, you can save yourself. At the end of the book, Hermione is never fully rewarded for her portion in saving Ron and Harry, just figuring out the riddle. Even after she was a better person than I.
                            <br>
                             *Quidditch and chess - not really my thing although this opened up a brilliant line of merchandising for the author.
                             <br>
                              *Some things didn't make sense to me. Why was there a sip of the potions left? Why exactly was Dudley so popular at school?
                              <br>
                               <br>
                                Now, I think a trip to Orlando is in order to visit the Wizarding World of Harry Potter!
                                <br>
                                 <br>

                <div class="left bodycol">
                 <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
                  <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1530857?book_show_action=true">
                   May 29, 2007
                  </a>
                  <span itemprop="author" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
                   <a class="user" href="/user/show/105351-harold-bloom" itemprop="url" name="Harold Bloom" title="Harold Bloom">
                    Harold Bloom
                   </a>

                  <span class="staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it">

                   </span>
                   <span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15">

                  <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
                   Shelves:
                   <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/105351-harold-bloom?shelf=therabblement">
                    therabblement
                   </a>
                  </div>

                 <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <span class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1530857">
                   <span id="freeTextContainer18013918664813384195">
                    <b>
                     Can 35 Million Book Buyers Be Wrong? Yes.
                    </b>
                    <br>
                     <br>
                      Taking arms against Harry Potter, at this moment, is to emulate Hamlet taking arms against a sea of troubles. By opposing the sea, you won't end it. The Harry Potter epiphenomenon will go on, doubtless for some time, as J. R. R. Tolkien did, and then wane.
                      <br>
                       <br>
                        The official newspaper of our dominant counter-culture, The New York Times, has been startled by the Potter books into establishing a new policy for its not very literate book review. Rather than crowd o
                       </br>
                      </br>
                     </br>
                    </br>
                   </span>
                   <span id="freeText18013918664813384195" style="display:none">
                    <b>
                     Can 35 Million Book Buyers Be Wrong? Yes.
                    </b>
                    <br>
                     <br>
                      Taking arms against Harry Potter, at this moment, is to emulate Hamlet taking arms against a sea of troubles. By opposing the sea, you won't end it. The Harry Potter epiphenomenon will go on, doubtless for some time, as J. R. R. Tolkien did, and then wane.
                      <br>
                       <br>
                        The official newspaper of our dominant counter-culture, The New York Times, has been startled by the Potter books into establishing a new policy for its not very literate book review. Rather than crowd out the Grishams, Clancys, Crichtons, Kings, and other vastly popular prose fictions on its fiction bestseller list, the Potter volumes will now lead a separate children's list. J. K. Rowling, the chronicler of Harry Potter, thus has an unusual distinction: She has changed the policy of the policy-maker.
                        <br>
                         <br>
                          Imaginative Vision
                          <br>
                           <br>
                            I read new children's literature, when I can find some of any value, but had not tried Rowling until now. I have just concluded the 300 pages of the first book in the series, "Harry Potter and the Sorcerer's Stone," purportedly the best of the lot. Though the book is not well written, that is not in itself a crucial liability. It is much better to see the movie, "The Wizard of Oz," than to read the book upon which it was based, but even the book possessed an authentic imaginative vision. "Harry Potter and the Sorcerer's Stone" does not, so that one needs to look elsewhere for the book's (and its sequels') remarkable success. Such speculation should follow an account of how and why Harry Potter asks to be read.
                            <br>
                             <br>
                              The ultimate model for Harry Potter is "Tom Brown's School Days" by Thomas Hughes, published in 1857. The book depicts the Rugby School presided over by the formidable Thomas Arnold, remembered now primarily as the father of Matthew Arnold, the Victorian critic-poet. But Hughes' book, still quite readable, was realism, not fantasy. Rowling has taken "Tom Brown's School Days" and re-seen it in the magical mirror of Tolkein. The resultant blend of a schoolboy ethos with a liberation from the constraints of reality-testing may read oddly to me, but is exactly what millions of children and their parents desire and welcome at this time.
                              <br>
                               <br>
                                In what follows, I may at times indicate some of the inadequacies of "Harry Potter." But I will keep in mind that a host are reading it who simply will not read superior fare, such as Kenneth Grahame's "The Wind in the Willows" or the "Alice" books of Lewis Carroll. Is it better that they read Rowling than not read at all? Will they advance from Rowling to more difficult pleasures?
                                <br>
                                 <br>
                                  Rowling presents two Englands, mundane and magical, divided not by social classes, but by the distinction between the "perfectly normal" (mean and selfish) and the adherents of sorcery. The sorcerers indeed seem as middle-class as the Muggles, the name the witches and wizards give to the common sort, since those addicted to magic send their sons and daughters off to Hogwarts, a Rugby school where only witchcraft and wizardry are taught. Hogwarts is presided over by Albus Dumbeldore as Headmaster, he being Rowling's version of Tolkein's Gandalf. The young future sorcerers are just like any other budding Britons, only more so, sports and food being primary preoccupations. (Sex barely enters into Rowling's cosmos, at least in the first volume.)
                                  <br>
                                   <br>
                                    ----------------------------
                                    <br>
                                     <br>
                                      The first half of a little piece I wrote from the
                                      <i>
                                       Journal
                                      </i>
                                      in July 2000. Rest is available at [
                                      <a href="http://wrt-brooke.syr.edu/courses/205.03/bloom.html" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank">
                                       http://wrt-brooke.syr.edu/courses/205...
                                      </a>
                                      ].
                                     </br>
                                    </br>
